WHY (P0): a beta tester reported the front page shows yesterday's daily pick as a WIN every day — they saw PHI featured + lose, yet "Yesterday" still showed a win. This FABRICATES a winning track record → directly destroys the transparency wedge (gtm §1). Fix immediately + honestly (an honest LOSS shown builds more trust than a fake win).
ROOT CAUSE (two compounding bugs, both confirmed):
 (1) BACKEND cherry-picks a winner — `_FEATURED_YESTERDAY_SERVING_SQL` (scripts/write_serving_store.py ~L888) ends `ORDER BY actual_outcome DESC NULLS LAST ... LIMIT 1`, so among ALL of yesterday's picks it surfaces whichever WON (actual_outcome=1), not the pick that was actually FEATURED. It also qualifies on `qualified_bet = TRUE` while the TODAY query (`_FEATURED_TODAY_SERVING_SQL` ~L830) selects on `layer4_h2h_conviction_flag = TRUE` + earliest `game_datetime ASC LIMIT 1` → the two don't even identify the same pick.
 (2) FRONTEND hardcodes the win badge — `app/page.tsx` renders the "Yesterday" badge as emerald (`bg-[#10b981]`) + `<CheckCircle2/>` UNCONDITIONALLY, regardless of `pick.yesterday.outcome` → even a "Loss" string shows green with a ✓.
FIX:
 (a) BACKEND: make "yesterday" track the SAME pick that was featured — reuse the EXACT today-selection logic (the `_FEATURED_TODAY_SERVING_SQL` ranking: conviction-flag qualifier, market-data/post_lineup tiebreak, earliest `game_datetime ASC LIMIT 1`) but for `DATEADD(day,-1,today)`, then LEFT JOIN `mart_clv_labeled_games` for that pick's REAL `actual_outcome`. Remove the `ORDER BY actual_outcome DESC` cherry-pick entirely. Emit an honest outcome status: win / loss / push / pending(actual_outcome NULL = not yet settled). Confirm `actual_outcome` semantics = the BET result for the picked side (team won / over hit), not CLV-positive — if it's CLV-based, use the true game/total result instead (a CLV-positive loss must still read "Loss" to the user).
 (b) FRONTEND: branch the badge on the real outcome — win→emerald + ✓, loss→red + ✗ (e.g. XCircle), push→neutral, pending/unsettled→neutral "Pending" or hide the badge (NEVER default to win). Update the `YesterdayResult` type if a status enum is added.
GUARD: a clean sample where yesterday's featured pick LOST must render red "Loss"; a win renders green; an unsettled game renders pending — verify all three.
Read: scripts/write_serving_store.py (`_FEATURED_TODAY_SERVING_SQL` L830, `_FEATURED_YESTERDAY_SERVING_SQL` L888, the "Build yesterday result" block ~L1808) + frontend/app/page.tsx (YesterdayResult type L25 + the badge render ~L267-280) + mart_clv_labeled_games (actual_outcome definition).
Gate/AC: yesterday's badge reflects the ACTUAL featured pick's REAL result (win/loss/push/pending), selected by the same logic as today; no cherry-pick; frontend badge color/icon/text branch on outcome; QA all three states; `uv run pytest` + frontend build green. **Changelog entry (user-facing fix).**
Closeout (per §0.1): CI green + ⏭️ operator handoff (run-order + git add: write_serving_store.py + app/page.tsx + any type) + the changelog line + what to verify after deploy (load the front page, confirm a known recent loss shows red).

▶ Story prompt — INC-16-P2 Serving cache: Railway Postgres → DynamoDB   [Infra + App/backend · 🧭 OPUS · depends on P1 ✅ · bake-off-EXEMPT (migration/wiring, not a predictive model)]   (2026-06-26, operator — from the P1 handoff)

1. **DynamoDB data model — ⚠️ FLAG FOR OPERATOR CONFIRMATION before building.** Default: a single table, **PK = `cache_key`**, attributes `value` (JSON string/Map), `is_permanent` (bool), `updated_at` (ISO/epoch). For LIST/RANGE reads (e.g. `picks/game/*`): pick ONE and confirm with the operator — (a) **structured PK/SK** (PK = the prefix e.g. `"picks/game"`, SK = the suffix e.g. `"{game_pk}"`) so a `Query` on PK returns the range, or (b) a **GSI** keyed for the prefix. Prefer (a) single-table PK/SK if the prefixes are clean (cheaper, no GSI projection cost). State the trade-off + your recommendation; do NOT silently pick.

New read order = **DynamoDB → S3** (drop the PG tier; S3 stays the fallback). Keep the interface stable so the routers (`picks.py`, game-detail, book-odds, performance) are unchanged.

▶ INC-16-P5   ✅ EXECUTED LIVE 2026-06-27 (built + deployed + verified end-to-end; all on `main`). VERIFIED: 3 CI checks green; CD proven end-to-end (OIDC→SSM→deploy ~1m success); auto-on-merge confirmed; branch protection on `main` requires the 3 checks.

(3) ⭐ **BOOTSTRAP PARADOX: `deploy.sh` can't deploy itself** — it's the thing that pulls `main`, so a new/edited `deploy.sh` needs ONE manual `git pull` on the box (via SSM) before CD uses it; pull-first self-heals thereafter. (4) box env: `OPENWEATHERMAP_API_KEY` dropped from `env.required` (optional WARN-tier weather fallback); `SERVING_CACHE_TABLE` set explicitly to `credence-prod-serving-cache` (HALT-tier; don't rely on the code default).

▶ INC-16-P5 — Orchestration CI/CD in GitHub (gate + auto-deploy future orchestration merges)   [Infra/DevOps · 🧭 OPUS · ✅ UNBLOCKED — P4 done (box owns live on `main`) · bake-off-EXEMPT]   (2026-06-26, operator)
WHY (the recurring footgun this kills): once the AWS box owns live orchestration, "a pipeline change isn't live until the codeloc redeploys off `main`" is a MANUAL step → `main` and the running box silently drift. ⭐ **PRIMARY FAILURE MODE P5 EXISTS TO PREVENT (proven repeatedly at P4 cutover): BAKED-IMAGE DRIFT — container code is `COPY`'d into the image, so a host `git pull` does NOT update a running container.** Multiple P4 ops ran stale code after a pull until the image was rebuilt. So the CD job's core job is **rebuild AND redeploy the affected images** (`up -d --build <svc>` / `--profile capture build`), never just `git pull`. Compile-only CI already let a runtime break through once (INC-15: W1d wrong-types passed `dbtf compile`, broke `dbt_daily_build` at runtime). And P2/P4 surfaced deploy-only failure modes CI never sees (PEM `\n`-newline; IMDSv2 hop-limit; region-less boto3; **empty-but-present/missing env vars** — see env-parity below). This story makes orchestration merges self-gating + self-deploying so neither drift nor those traps recur.
SCOPE = a GitHub Actions workflow triggered on changes to the orchestration paths (`pipeline/**`, `services/dagster/aws/**`, `services/dbt_runner/**`, the capture-Lambda paths, `infrastructure/**`).
TASKS:
1. **CI gate (on PRs touching those paths)** — beyond the existing Python fast gate + dbt-Build jobs: (a) **Dagster `dagster definitions validate`** (defs actually LOAD — catches import/boot breaks like the observed `_InactiveRpcError` + the INC-15-class runtime break that compile missed); (b) **`docker compose -f services/dagster/aws/docker-compose.yml config`** + a BUILD of the changed images (catches the buildx/AL2023 + Dockerfile breaks); (c) a **lint/assert that the deploy wiring is present** — `_normalize_pem` applied wherever `SNOWFLAKE_PRIVATE_KEY` is consumed (resources/__init__.py, write_serving_store.py, dbt_runner entrypoint, every Snowflake-touching capture Lambda), `AWS_DEFAULT_REGION` set in the container/Lambda env, and no reintroduced `DATABASE_URL`/PG reference on serving/capture paths.
1d. **🔑 ENV-PARITY CHECK (would have caught EVERY P4 env gap pre-deploy).** Maintain a canonical key list (the keys the ops actually read) and assert the box `.env` contains every one — non-empty. P4 lost cycles to FOUR missing/empty vars (`ARTIFACTS_FROM_S3`, `CACHE_BUCKET`, `USER_BETS_TABLE`, `USERS_TABLE`) that each failed silently or late (⚠️ recall: empty-but-present shadows the code default — treat `KEY=` as MISSING, not set). The check: grep the ops for `os.environ.get`/`os.environ[` reads → diff against the box `.env` (or a committed `env.required` manifest) → fail the gate on any missing/empty required key. This + the IAM-grant manifest (the P4 inline policies `credence-s3-api-cache-rw`, `credence-dynamo-user-bets-settle`) should be documented so a fresh box has the full env+IAM set.
2. **CD (on merge to `main`, same paths)** — deploy to the box via SSH or SSM Run Command: `git pull` on `main` → `docker compose up -d --build` **AND `docker compose --profile capture build`** (the 4 host-cron captures are a separate profile — a plain `up --build` won't rebuild them, so capture-entrypoint changes won't take effect) → **post-deploy verification**: codeloc defs loaded, daemon up, `dbt-runner /health`={"ok":true}, `head -1 /tmp/snowflake_rsa_key.pem`=`-----BEGIN`, IMDS hop-limit=2 still set. Fail the job loudly (don't leave a half-deploy) if any check fails. Result: `main` == running box automatically — the manual codeloc redeploy is GONE.
2a. **Host-cron is NOT reloaded by a git pull.** `capture.crontab` is a tracked file; a change to it requires re-running `crontab capture.crontab` on the box — a `git pull` alone does NOT reinstall the host crontab. The CD job must detect a `capture.crontab` change and re-install it (then a no-op otherwise). (Post-P4 the box's copy == committed, so this is clean.)
2b. **Safe-deploy / blue-green (Railway gave us rolling deploys; replace it — PHASED).** ⚠️ Scope note: user-facing SERVING is decoupled from this box (frontend → Lambda → DynamoDB/S3), so a box redeploy does NOT take the site down — what we're protecting is (a) a bad deploy crash-looping a service and (b) killing an in-flight run. Also the Dagster **daemon/scheduler is a singleton** — never run two daemons at once (double-run hazard, same as the Dagster+∥box overlap) → any blue/green ends in a brief single-owner daemon handoff, not seamless N+1.
   - **NOW (do as part of this story, ~$0):** health-GATED deploy with **auto-rollback** — tag/keep the previous image; if the post-deploy checks (step 2) fail, revert to the prior tag instead of leaving it broken. Add a **graceful drain** before recreate: pause the `QueuedRunCoordinator` queue + let in-flight runs finish (or rely on run-retries) so a deploy doesn't sever a live run.
   - **EVENTUAL (defer — gated on an uptime SLA, post-beta; do NOT build now):** true blue/green — Caddy/ALB-fronted dual stacks for the stateless tier (webserver + code location) with a daemon-ownership handoff, or a standby instance to flip to. Cost ≈ a doubled compute footprint during deploys (or a standby box). Flag as a follow-up, not in-scope for the beta.
3. **Secrets/access** — use GitHub Actions OIDC → an AWS deploy role (no long-lived keys in CI); SSM Run Command preferred over raw SSH (no inbound 22 from GitHub, no key management). ⛔ Claude does NOT enter/handle any credential — the operator wires the OIDC trust + secrets; the prompt specifies WHAT, the operator provisions.
3a. **Reproducible-box bootstrap (so a fresh box isn't bitten by the P3 gotchas):** fold into cloud-init/provision — install + enable cron (`dnf install -y cronie && systemctl enable --now crond`; AL2023 minimal ships NO cron → P3 hit `crontab: command not found`), set IMDSv2 hop-limit=2, `AWS_DEFAULT_REGION`, install the `capture.crontab`, and the buildx≥0.17 fix. A rebuilt/replacement box should come up fully wired with zero manual steps. **🛠️ ALSO pull in INC-16-P7 task 1 here — PIN all compose image tags (kill `:latest`, esp. `flaresolverr:latest`) before wiring auto-`--build`**, else this CD can pull a breaking upstream image onto the live box silently.
4. **Branch protection** — require the new CI gate (+ the existing fast gate + dbt jobs) on PRs to `main` for orchestration paths.
CONVENTIONS: do NOT git commit/push (operator); the workflow file lands under `.github/workflows/`; keep it scoped to orchestration paths so app/model PRs aren't slowed.
AC: orchestration-path PRs are CI-gated (defs-validate + compose-build + deploy-wiring asserts, on top of fast gate + dbt jobs); merges to `main` on those paths auto-deploy to the box + self-verify (health + defs + key + IMDS) and **auto-rollback to the prior image on failure** + graceful-drain in-flight runs before recreate; OIDC/SSM access (no static keys, operator-provisioned); branch protection updated; the manual "codeloc redeploy off main" step is eliminated. (True blue/green = a flagged follow-up, not in this story.) Operator handoff with the OIDC/SSM setup steps + the `git add .github/workflows/...` list.
```
```
▶ INC-16-P6   ✅ EXECUTED LIVE 2026-06-28 (built + deployed via the P5 CD + emails CONFIRMED received). Box now PAGES instead of failing silently — closes the last soak risk. 🔥 **DISCOVERY that reframed it: post-P4 the ENTIRE legacy alert stack was SILENT** — every sensor notified by raising → Dagster+ Cloud's email-on-failure, which the cutover turned OFF → all alerts had been vanishing since cutover. P6 re-establishes the email path under self-hosted OSS + re-arms them. SHIPPED (6 layers → 1 SNS inbox): (1) 🪦 OFF-box dead-man Lambda `credence-deadman-daily` + EventBridge 08:30 ET reads a daily heartbeat `write_serving_store` writes to DynamoDB (`pk=ops,sk=heartbeat#daily`, best-effort; heartbeat > raw pick-count so a 0-pick off-day ≠ dead box); (2) CloudWatch alarms (status/mem>85%/swap>50%/disk>85%/CPU>90%-30m-sustained/credits-per-billing-mode); (3) host-cron service-liveness healthcheck (5 min, 1h cooldown, 7 containers + dagit/dbt-runner/flaresolverr); (4) OSS `run_failure_alert_sensor`→SNS LOUD for HALT-tier; (5) revived 5 raise-to-alert sensors → `send_alert` direct + `check_data_freshness` via crontab; (6) deploy.sh pages on auto-rollback. Shared `pipeline/utils/alerting.py` (soft-fail, never raises, 1h rate-limit) + `notify.sh`. VERIFIED: direct channel email ✅; healthcheck end-to-end (stopped flaresolverr → email ✅); CD deployed it; CW agent running. CI: 680 passed, defs-validate green (11 sensors), env-parity 21 keys. 🔑 gotchas: instance role intentionally lacks `ssm:SendCommand` (edit `.env`/sudo on-box, don't self-send); `docker compose` needs `-f services/dagster/aws/docker-compose.yml`; set `ALERT_SNS_TOPIC_ARN` on box BEFORE the merge (env.required) + start CW agent AFTER; healthcheck has a 1h file cooldown (`rm /tmp/credence_healthcheck_last_alert` before re-test). ▶ INC-16-P6 — Observability + email alerting for the AWS orchestration box   [Infra/SRE · 🧭 OPUS · ✅ DONE — was the last INC-16 recovery story · bake-off-EXEMPT]   (2026-06-26, operator)
WHY: the box (EC2 `i-07594af1679f81c38`) now runs the live daily cycle + host-cron captures (P5 CI/CD live, schedules ON, Dagster+ OFF) with NO alerting → a silent failure (dead box, crashed daemon, failed build, bad deploy) wouldn't surface until someone notices stale picks. 🪝 Hook the now-live P5 CD `deploy.sh` verify path too (a failed deploy/auto-rollback should alert). 🔭 The whole INC-16 build proved serving degrades SILENTLY (P5 even found `SERVING_CACHE_TABLE` empty; P4 found `CACHE_BUCKET` silent-skip) → outcome-based alerting is the soak safety net. Add layered observability, **email preferred** (SES is already wired). All ~$0 (CloudWatch alarms ~$0.10/alarm/mo; SNS email + SES effectively free at beta volume). "Dagster goes down" = 3 distinct failure modes → one layer each:
TASKS:
1. **🪦 DAILY-OUTPUT DEAD-MAN'S SWITCH (highest value — do FIRST; outcome-based, catches ALL root causes).** Alert if today's picks aren't in the DynamoDB serving cache (`credence-prod-serving-cache`) by a cutoff (e.g. 8:00am ET). This fires whether the cause was a dead box, a failed dbt build, a bad deploy, or a stuck daemon — it watches the THING USERS SEE, not a process. Implement as a small scheduled check (Lambda+EventBridge, or a CloudWatch metric + "no-data" alarm fed by `write_serving_store` emitting a success metric/heartbeat) → SES/SNS email on miss. ⚠️ Finalize the cutoff + the "today produced" definition once P4 makes the box own the full daily cycle; the check itself can be built now against the current output.
   - 🔬 **WHY this is THE priority (P4 proved serving degrades SILENTLY):** `write_serving_store` skips ALL S3-fallback writes on a missing `CACHE_BUCKET` (`if bucket:` — no error), and WARN-tier settlement swallows errors. Process/health checks would have stayed GREEN while the output silently rotted. Outcome-based alerting (picks present in DynamoDB by cutoff; `mart_odds_outcomes` ingestion_ts advancing) is the ONLY thing that surfaces this class without a human noticing → build #1 and the capture-staleness check (#5) FIRST.
2. **📉 BOX / INSTANCE LIVENESS + RESOURCE PRESSURE** — CloudWatch **EC2 status-check alarms** (instance + system reachability) → SNS topic → email subscription (catches instance death / unreachable). Plus resource alarms tuned for this **burstable t4g.medium (2 vCPU, 4 GB, baseline ~40% combined)** — calibrated so normal daily-build/predict bursts DON'T page, only genuine trouble:
   - **🧠 MEMORY/SWAP (highest-value on this box — OOM is the likeliest failure, not CPU):** CloudWatch agent `mem_used_percent` > **85%** for 10 min, AND swap-in-use climbing / `swap_used_percent` > ~50% → alarm. (The 4 GB box OOM'd heavy PyMC/CatBoost builds before the swapfile; an OOM kills a process outright vs. CPU just slowing.) Pair with a quick `dmesg | grep -i oom` note in the runbook line.
   - **💽 DISK:** root `disk_used_percent` > **85%** (Docker images/logs/parquet temp fill a small root vol).
   - **🔥 CPU — alarm on SUSTAINED, not spikes:** `CPUUtilization` > **90% for 30 min** (3 consecutive 10-min datapoints) → investigate. ⚠️ Do NOT alarm on brief 80–100% spikes — the daily build / `predict_today` / image rebuilds / FanGraphs solves are *expected* minutes-long bursts. The real signal is high CPU **sustained for hours outside a known build window** (baseline is 40%; load average sustained > 2 on the 2 vCPUs = saturated).
   - **🎟️ CPU CREDITS:** if the instance is `standard` mode, alarm `CPUCreditBalance` < **50** (throttle precursor). If `unlimited` (the t4g default — confirm via `describe-instance-credit-specifications`), skip the balance alarm and instead watch `CPUSurplusCreditsCharged` trending up (cost, not throttle). At beta volume neither should fire from routine serving; a sustained breach = a runaway process or a heavy retrain mistakenly run on this serving box.
3. **🐳 SERVICE LIVENESS (box up but a container down/daemon not ticking — a plain ping misses this)** — a host-cron healthcheck (~every 5 min) asserting `docker compose ps` all-Up + `curl` dagit:3000 + dbt-runner:8080/health + flaresolverr:8191; on failure publish to SNS/SES. Optionally also alarm on the Dagster daemon heartbeat going stale (the daemon can be "up" but stop ticking schedules/sensors).
4. **🚨 DAGSTER RUN-FAILURE ALERTS** — wire a Dagster OSS `run_failure_sensor` → **SES email**, scoped LOUD to the **HALT-tier** ops (per the CLAUDE.md E11.7 op→tier map: predict_today, dbt_daily_build run-step, write_serving_store, signal_freshness_check, ingest_statcast, the W1 lakehouse ops, …) so serving-critical failures shout; WARN-tier failures can be digest/suppressed to avoid noise.
5. **♻️ REUSE existing signals, don't reinvent** — audit `scripts/check_data_freshness.py` + `signal_freshness_check` (already in the repo) and ROUTE their output to the same SES/SNS channel rather than building parallel freshness logic. Note the host-cron captures (P3) too — alert if odds capture stops landing in `mart_odds_outcomes` (a capture-specific dead-man switch, since they're host-cron not Dagster-monitored).
6. **Alert hygiene** — one SNS topic (or a couple by severity), de-duped/rate-limited so a flapping box doesn't spam; a clear subject convention (`[Credence PROD] …`); a documented runbook line per alert (what it means + first action). Record the alarms + topic + SES identity in `infrastructure/aws_resources.md`.
⛔ Claude does NOT enter credentials / confirm SES identities / subscribe email addresses — the operator confirms the SNS email subscription + any SES sender identity; the prompt specifies WHAT, the operator provisions. CONVENTIONS: do NOT git commit/push (operator); honest framing; >1-min scripts to the operator.
AC: a verified email arrives for each layer — (a) the daily-output dead-man switch (simulate a missed write), (b) instance unreachable / disk-full / **memory-pressure (OOM precursor)**, (c) a stopped container, (d) a HALT-tier run failure; **the burstable-tuned resource alarms in place (mem>85%+swap, disk>85%, CPU>90%-for-30min, CPU-credit balance/surplus per mode) — calibrated so normal build bursts don't page**; existing freshness checks routed to the same channel; capture-feed staleness alerts; alerts de-duped + documented in `aws_resources.md`. Operator handoff with the SNS/SES setup steps + the `git add` list (the healthcheck script, the sensor, any Lambda, the alarm definitions/IaC).

▶ INC-16-P7 — Dependency / upgrade & patch management for the self-hosted stack   [Infra/SRE · 🧭 OPUS · 🔵 STANDALONE non-critical (de-scoped from incident-critical 2026-06-28) · rides on the live P5 CI/CD + P6 alerting + CD auto-rollback as the upgrade net · bake-off-EXEMPT]   (2026-06-26, operator)
WHY: leaving Railway/Dagster+ moved version + security-patch ownership to us. Self-hosted Dagster, dbt-runner, flaresolverr, the metadata Postgres, the OS (AL2023), and all Docker base images + Python deps now need deliberate, tested upgrades — and CVEs need to not sit unnoticed. Make upgrades reproducible + reviewed (not something that lands by accident on the next deploy).
TASKS:
1. **🛠️ PIN EVERYTHING.** ✅ PARTIAL — P5 already pinned **`flaresolverr` off `:latest`**. REMAINING: audit every OTHER image tag in `services/dagster/aws/docker-compose.yml` (+ the capture profile) and pin to explicit versions, ideally `@sha256` digests — confirm no remaining `:latest`. (P5's CD auto-runs `up --build`, so any `:latest` could pull a breaking upstream image onto the LIVE box silently → pinned = deliberate.) Pin Python deps too (the lockfile is the source of truth; confirm the code image builds from it, not floating).
2. **🧩 Dagster version-coupling discipline (document as a runbook).** Dagster requires the daemon + webserver + code-location + the installed `dagster` Python lib to ALL be the SAME version (mixed = broken gRPC/schema). So a Dagster bump = a COORDINATED change across all four + a `dagster instance migrate` against the metadata Postgres, read the release notes for that version, and validate defs load BEFORE the live box. Write this as `services/dagster/aws/UPGRADING.md` (or a runbook section) so the next session doesn't bump one container in isolation.
3. **🤖 Automated update PRs.** Stand up Renovate (preferred) or Dependabot on the repo for the orchestration image tags + Python deps → it raises PRs that flow through the **P5 CI gate** (`dagster definitions validate` + compose-build catches a defs-breaking or unbuildable upgrade BEFORE merge). Group/schedule them (e.g. a weekly batch) so they're not noise; label so app/model deps aren't entangled with orchestration ones.
4. **🔒 Security-patch cadence.** Document a periodic (≈monthly) review: OS `dnf upgrade` on the box (or bake into a fresh AMI/cloud-init — pairs with P5's reproducible box → "replace the box" beats "patch in place"), base-image refresh, and a scan of the Renovate/Dependabot security alerts. Subscribe to Dagster release notes + GitHub security advisories for the pinned components so CVEs surface.
5. **🧪 Test path for upgrades.** An upgrade PR must be green on the P5 CI gate; for a Dagster MINOR/major bump (higher risk), validate on a throwaway/standby box (or the P5 EVENTUAL standby) before promoting to live, and rely on P5 auto-rollback + P6 alerting as the net. Don't promote an un-tested Dagster bump straight to the live daemon.
⛔ Claude does NOT enter credentials / GitHub-app installs — the operator installs Renovate/Dependabot + any registry creds; the prompt specifies WHAT. CONVENTIONS: do NOT git commit/push (operator); >1-min scripts to operator.
AC: all compose image tags pinned (no `:latest`; digests where practical) + Python deps pinned to the lockfile; `UPGRADING.md` documents the Dagster coordinated-bump + `instance migrate` rule; Renovate/Dependabot raising grouped orchestration-dep PRs that pass the P5 CI gate; a documented security-patch cadence + advisory subscriptions; an upgrade test path (CI-green + standby-validate for Dagster bumps). Operator handoff with the Renovate/Dependabot setup steps + the `git add` list (pinned compose, UPGRADING.md, renovate.json/dependabot.yml).

▶ INC-16-P8 — DEV/STAGING Dagster+dbt+data box for PR pipeline integration testing   [Infra/SRE · 🧭 OPUS · 🔵 STANDALONE 🔭 down-the-road (NOT beta-blocking; de-scoped from incident 2026-06-28) · extends the now-LIVE P5 CI/CD ✅ · bake-off-EXEMPT]   (2026-06-26, operator)
NOTE (P5 now live): the P5 CD (`orchestration_cd.yml` → OIDC→SSM→`deploy.sh`) + CI gate exist — P8 slots in as a HIGHER gate: a PR-diff-scoped pipeline RUN on the dev box, hung off the same workflow. The dev box also doubles as P7's Dagster-upgrade test box + the deferred P5 blue/green standby (one box, three jobs).
WHY: P5's CI gate is STRUCTURAL (`dagster definitions validate` + `docker compose build` + `dbtf compile`) — it proves things load/build but does NOT RUN a pipeline against real-shaped data. That's exactly the gap that caused INC-15: W1d's wrong data-types passed `dbtf compile` and only broke at RUNTIME. A dev box that executes the AFFECTED pipeline end-to-end against real-ish data catches runtime/data-shape breaks no compile step can. This is the next TIER above P5, not a duplicate.
💡 ONE BOX, THREE JOBS — scope a single dev/staging box that also serves as (a) P7's Dagster-upgrade test box and (b) P5's EVENTUAL blue/green standby. That turns a "second environment" into well-justified shared infra (don't spec three separate boxes).
TASKS:
1. **Provision a dev box** (reuse the P5 reproducible-box cloud-init so it's identical to prod minus data targets). Cost-shape — pick + flag for operator: (a) **ephemeral spin-up-on-PR** (CI launches it / a spot instance only while a pipeline PR is open, runs the test, tears down → ~$0; preferred for beta); (b) a **dedicated always-on small box** (~$25/mo) that doubles as the P7 upgrade-test + P5 standby; (c) ⛔ reuse the PROD box with a dev Compose project — cheapest but risks contention with live orchestration + weak isolation → avoid.
2. **🔒 DATA ISOLATION (the real design work — get this right or it's dangerous).** The integration run reads a SAMPLED/sandboxed dataset and writes ONLY to **dev targets** — a dev Snowflake schema, a dev S3 prefix, a dev DynamoDB table — and must NEVER touch prod serving (`mart_odds_outcomes`, `credence-prod-serving-cache`) or prod marts. 3. **Affected-pipeline selection from the PR diff** — only run what the PR touches: dbt `state:modified+` (using the prod-manifest baseline like CI already does, per the E11.16 `scripts/dbt_state.sh` pattern) + the changed `pipeline/` ops. Don't run the whole DAG on every PR.
4. **Wire into P5's CI/CD** — on a PR touching pipeline/dbt paths, after the structural gate passes: deploy the PR branch to the dev box → run the selected pipeline(s) against dev data → assert success + basic output sanity (rows landed, no type errors) → report status back on the PR → (if ephemeral) tear down. This becomes a higher gate that would have caught W1d.
5. **Guardrails** — the dev run must be unable to write prod (verify with a dry-run/IAM scoping); dev box IAM role grants dev-target access only (no prod serving write). Document the env in `aws_resources.md`.
⛔ Claude does NOT enter credentials / provision IAM — the operator wires the dev IAM role + any spot/launch perms; the prompt specifies WHAT. CONVENTIONS: do NOT git commit/push (operator); >1-min scripts to operator.
AC: a dev box (ephemeral-on-PR or shared standby) reproducible from the P5 cloud-init; a sampled dev dataset in ISOLATED dev Snowflake/S3/DynamoDB targets with NO path to prod serving; PR-diff-scoped pipeline selection (dbt state:modified+ + changed ops); CI runs the affected pipeline end-to-end on the dev box + reports PR status; verified-isolation guardrail (dev run cannot write prod). Operator handoff with the dev-IAM/launch setup + the `git add` list.

▶ E9.34   ✅ BOTH BUGS FIXED + VERIFIED (Sonnet, 2026-06-28; operator-confirmed post-deploy). 
 • **BUG 1 (EV times +5h) — RENDER layer:** `stg_statsapi_games.game_date` is TIMESTAMP_TZ → Pydantic v2 serializes as `...+00:00` (OFFSET, not `Z`). The prior partial fix's `endsWith("Z")` check missed the offset case → appended Z → invalid `"...+00:00Z"` → browser parsed as LOCAL. Fix: `formatGameTime` now uses the string as-is if it ends in `Z` OR matches `/[+-]\d\d:?\d\d$/`, else appends Z (mirrors game-detail `fmtGameTime`); covers all 3 EV call sites. Dashboard was immune — it uses a SERVER-side `game_time_et` (`_format_game_time_et`), never parses `game_start_utc` client-side.
 • **BUG 2 (ATL@SF stuck pending) — settle filter:** MLB Stats API has TWO terminal codes — `'F'` (Final) and `'O'` (Final/Official, after the official scorer; LATE games are usually `'O'` by the nightly settle run). `_final_scores()` in `settle_user_bets.py` queried `status_code = 'F'` only → `'O'` games invisible → bet stuck pending forever. Fix: `WHERE status_code IN ('F','O')`. TZ hypothesis RULED OUT (settle queries by `game_pk`, not date → UTC day boundaries irrelevant).
 Files: `frontend/app/ev-tracker/page.tsx`, `scripts/settle_user_bets.py`, `changelog.json` (2 entries, `2026-06-22` block). CI: tsc + fast gate 683 + changelog-guard green.
 🔑 DURABLE LESSONS: (a) **Pydantic v2 serializes tz-aware datetimes as `±offset`, NOT `Z`** → any frontend date parsing must handle BOTH (or better, serve a server-side pre-formatted string like Dashboard's `game_time_et` — the robust pattern); (b) settle on `('F','O')`, not `'F'` alone. ⚠️ **PM FOLLOW-UP owed:** the `'F'`-only bug was PRE-EXISTING (not cutover) → OTHER late games all season may have bets STILL stuck pending → run a one-off re-settle sweep (the fixed job re-queries pending-by-GSI → should clear them). (Orig prompt ↓.)
▶ Story prompt — E9.34 P1 BUG: EV Tracker game times shifted +5h (one TZ offset) — Dashboard is CORRECT   [App · 🔴 P1 TRUST · 🧭 OPUS · frontend + serving — diagnose before fixing]   (2026-06-28, operator; screenshot-reported)
WHY (P1 trust): the EV Tracker shows wrong game start times on a BETTING page — and the page's own banner tells users "don't bet until confirmed lineups ~90 min before first pitch," so a wrong time can actively mislead a bet. Fix honestly + at the right layer.
🔑 **THE DIAGNOSTIC LEVER (use this — it narrows the search hugely):** the SAME game renders DIFFERENTLY on two pages. MIA @ STL on **Dashboard = `1:15 PM CDT` (CORRECT)**; on **EV Tracker = `6:15 PM CDT` (WRONG)**. Δ = **+5h = exactly the CDT UTC offset (UTC−5)** → the EV Tracker is doing ONE FEWER UTC→local conversion (rendering an 18:15 UTC value as if it were 18:15 local = 6:15 PM). **Because the DASHBOARD is correct, the upstream data is almost certainly FINE** (MLB schedule → the W3pre-migrated `stg_statsapi_games` → the marts → serving) → **this is most likely NOT a W3pre/data regression; it's an EV-tracker-specific FIELD or FORMATTER issue.** Don't burn the session chasing the lakehouse.
GROUNDED POINTERS (already inspected):
 • EV page render: `frontend/app/ev-tracker/page.tsx` — `formatGameTime(isoString)` (~L199) appends `'Z'` to force-UTC-parse a naive timestamp, then `toLocaleTimeString` (browser→CDT). Called at ~L268, ~L1279, ~L1348. The field is **`pick.game_start_utc`**; the DATE is a SEPARATE field `pick.game_date` (rendered at `T12:00:00` local). ⚠️ A `formatGameTime` UTC-fix JUST shipped (W3pre session) yet EV still shows the buggy +5h time → either the fix doesn't cover the EV payload's actual string FORMAT (e.g. space-separated `"2026-06-28 18:15:00"` vs `T`-separated → `+Z` may not force UTC in the browser), or a render path/value it doesn't reach.
 • Dashboard render (the CORRECT one): `frontend/app/page.tsx` — find ITS game-time formatter + which field it reads. **DIFF the two: same field? same string format? same formatter logic?** The delta between them IS the bug.
 • Serving writer: `scripts/write_serving_store.py` — ⚠️ it aliases **`g.game_date AS game_start_utc`** in some CTEs (~L217, ~L311) BUT also carries a real **`b.game_start_utc`** from `mart_game_odds_bridge` (which derives from `commence_time`) in others (~L254/280/318/336). **So different serving payloads populate `game_start_utc` DIFFERENTLY — a real start-timestamp vs a date-at-midnight.** Determine EXACTLY which payload/field the EV-tracker endpoint serves vs what the Dashboard serves; an aliased-`game_date` (midnight) or a `commence_time` with a different format/precision is a prime suspect.
 • Backend: `app/backend/routers/picks.py` + `app/backend/models/picks.py` — how `game_start_utc` is serialized (does it emit a `Z`/offset, a naive NTZ string, `T`- vs space-separated?). The serialized STRING FORMAT is what makes `formatGameTime`'s `+Z` work or fail.
DEBUG ORDER (reproduce → isolate → diagnose → fix; engineering:debug discipline):
 1. **Capture the raw value at each layer for one game (MIA@STL, 2026-06-28):** the DynamoDB serving payload (`credence-prod-serving-cache`) for BOTH the EV-tracker key AND the dashboard key → record the exact `game_start_utc` string each carries (S3 fallback too if relevant). Ground truth: MLB has it at 18:15 UTC = 1:15 PM CDT.
 2. **Isolate where they diverge:** is the EV payload's value already wrong (a date / different format / different field), or is the value identical to the dashboard's but the EV FORMATTER mishandles it? That single comparison tells you DATA-layer vs RENDER-layer.
 3. **Diagnose the format:** if both carry `18:15`-ish UTC but EV renders +5h, it's the render (formatGameTime's `+Z` not forcing UTC for that string format) → fix the formatter to robustly parse to UTC (normalize `T`/space, ensure a single UTC→local conversion; mirror the Dashboard's working formatter). If EV's value is a `game_date`-midnight alias or a differently-typed `commence_time`, fix it at `write_serving_store` (serve the real start timestamp in a consistent UTC ISO format) — ⚠️ serving-write path runs on the AWS box (INC-16) → land via the P5 CD, verify post-deploy.
 4. **Pick the RIGHT layer:** prefer normalizing the SERVED format to a single canonical UTC ISO (`...Z`) so every consumer (EV, dashboard, game-detail `picks/[game_pk]` `fmtGameTime`) renders identically — then the frontend formatters don't each need their own `+Z` hack.
SECONDARY (note, don't rabbit-hole): the first screenshot shows games tagged "Confirmed" under a "Preliminary predictions — lineups not yet confirmed" banner — flag whether that's a related state/staleness inconsistency or independent; report, fix only if same root cause.
Read: the 4 files above + `frontend/app/picks/[game_pk]/page.tsx` (`fmtGameTime` — the reference the EV fix cited) + `mart_game_odds_bridge.sql` (commence_time→game_start_utc).
Gate/AC: EV Tracker game times MATCH the Dashboard AND MLB ground truth (MIA@STL → 1:15 PM CDT) across all market sections (Moneyline/Totals/etc.) + the Line Shopping tab; root cause named at a SPECIFIC layer (data vs render) with the raw before/after value; fix at the source (ideally a canonical served UTC format consumed identically everywhere); `tsc --noEmit` + fast gate green; **changelog entry (user-facing trust fix, Monday-bucketed)**. If the fix touches `write_serving_store`, verify on a real serving write + the live page post-deploy.
Closeout (§0.1): ⏭️ operator handoff — the layer-by-layer raw values (DynamoDB EV vs dashboard vs MLB), the root-cause layer, `git add` list, changelog line, post-deploy verify (load EV Tracker, confirm times == Dashboard). Keep separate from any W3-main/zone_matchup work.

━━━ ADDENDUM (2026-06-28, operator) — 🐞 SECOND BUG, likely SAME TZ root cause: a settled game shows UNSETTLED on the Bet Log ━━━
SYMPTOM: an **ATL @ SF** bet is NOT showing as settled on the Bet Log, though the game was **LAST NIGHT**. Investigate WHILE you're in the date/time code — there's a strong chance it shares E9.34's UTC-date mishandling.
🔑 WHY IT MAY BE THE SAME BUG: **ATL @ SF is a Pacific-time (late) game** — a ~7pm PT first pitch is **~02:xx UTC the NEXT day**. If any date logic in the settle/results path buckets by **UTC date**, a late West-coast game rolls into the next UTC day → it gets mis-dated → the settle job looks for its result on the wrong date (or treats it as "not yet played") → the bet stays PENDING. That's the exact class of UTC-vs-local error E9.34 is about. **Test this hypothesis first.**
HOW SETTLEMENT WORKS (grounded): bets live in `credence-prod-dynamo-user-bets`; a PENDING bet carries `pending_game_pk` (= game_pk) on the sparse GSI **`gsi-pending-by-game`**; `scripts/settle_user_bets.py` queries that GSI, looks up the game RESULT, writes the outcome, and REMOVEs `pending_game_pk` (that removal = "settled"). The Bet Log `/bets` read surfaces the stored outcome. ⚠️ `settle_user_bets_op` is **WARN-tier** (CLAUDE.md op→tier map) → a failure logs a warning and the op SUCCEEDS → SILENT (and P6's `run_failure_alert_sensor` is LOUD only for HALT-tier, so it would NOT have paged).
DIAGNOSE — first split SYSTEMIC vs GAME-SPECIFIC:
 1. **Has ANY bet settled since the INC-16 cutover (06-27)?** If NONE → the settle job is broken on the new AWS box (systemic), NOT ATL/SF-specific. ⚠️ P4 Phase-G found `USER_BETS_TABLE` was empty-but-present on the box + added IAM `credence-dynamo-user-bets-settle` — verify those are correct AND that the settle op is actually SCHEDULED + RUNNING on the box (check its last run / Dagit). If OTHER bets settled but ATL/SF didn't → it's game-specific → go to step 2.
 2. **Inspect the ATL/SF bet item** in `credence-prod-dynamo-user-bets`: does it still carry `pending_game_pk`? what `game_pk` / `game_date`? Then check: is that game's **RESULT present** in the results source the settle job reads (`mart_game_results` / wherever `settle_user_bets.py` pulls the final outcome)? If the result is MISSING → either the results feed is lagging (note: `mart_odds_events` has been stale since 06-04 — a related feed lag is plausible) OR the game_pk/date filter mis-bucketed the late PT game (the TZ hypothesis).
 3. If TZ: fix the settle/results date handling COHERENTLY with E9.34's fix (one canonical UTC handling). ## 🏁 SNOWFLAKE DECOMMISSION PROGRAM — E11.1 W4 → reader-migration (the "Cortex-only" finish)   [Infra · cost · 🧭 OPUS-ONLY · all bake-off-EXEMPT]   (operator 2026-06-28: PUSH straight through, then Opus → model work)

🌐 **ENVIRONMENT REALITY (post-INC-16 — READ FIRST; applies to W4/W5/W6/W7):** We are **OFF Railway ENTIRELY** (the workspace was T&S-restricted → the plan is CANCELLED — there is no Railway). Orchestration = **self-hosted Dagster OSS on AWS EC2** (`i-07594af1679f81c38`); lakehouse builds run THERE via `run_w1_lakehouse_op` — **NEVER a "Railway cron."** The serving cache is **DynamoDB `credence-prod-serving-cache`** (P2 deleted the Postgres `api_cache` + `app/backend/services/pg.py` → `serving_cache.py`); **there is NO Postgres serving layer and NO `DATABASE_URL`** anywhere; serving read order = **DynamoDB → S3**. Cutover ships via the **P5 CD** (merge to `main` auto-deploys OIDC→SSM→`deploy.sh`, rebuilds on `dbt/**`+`scripts/**`; create the `lakehouse_ext` external tables BEFORE the merge). ⚠️ **Any older prompt/code/comment you read that mentions Railway, a Railway-cron, Railway PG, `DATABASE_URL`, or the PG `api_cache` is STALE — do NOT act on it; if you touch that code, strip/flag the stale reference.**
**SHARED MACHINERY (every wave reuses — DON'T reinvent; mirror W2/W3-main):** dual-branch model (`{% if target.name=='duckdb' %}` DuckDB transform over S3-views `{% else %}` thin `select * from baseball_data.lakehouse_ext.<model>`; `materialized='view', tags=['wN_lakehouse']`) · extend `run_w1_lakehouse.py` (a `W{N}_MART_MODELS` ordered list + `_build_w{N}` that registers each as a view immediately so intra-wave deps resolve) · `generate_w{N}_external_tables.py` (mirror the W3 generator; UPPERCASE cols) · `refresh_w1_external_tables.py` `W{N}_TABLES` in the HALT/required set · a `parity_check_w{N}.py` (game-grain = freshness-aware game_pk no-loss vs current stg; season-grain = row-count tolerance; PK-uniqueness HARD; column-hash WARN; reuse the stg integrity pre-flight).
**DuckDB-compat checklist (each verified, W3-main + W4):** `::number`→`::decimal(scale)` (explicit scale or values zero); `dateadd('day',n,d)`→`d + interval 'n days'`; `game_date::date` before any RANGE-window/interval (parquet stores it VARCHAR); a result-cast `(ratio)::numeric` is scale-0 in Snowflake (often DELIBERATELY zeroed) — REPRODUCE it, don't "fix" it; confirm every consumer of a zeroed col reads a different (rolling/std) col; **(W4) FanGraphs/big JSON flatten → set `threads=2` + a `memory_limit` (else OOM); httpfs → raise `http_timeout`; the live `pitcher_clusters` keys on `fit_date` (NOT `snapshot_date`), unique `(pitcher_id, season)`; hash WARNs on FLOAT cols = stringification artifact, not a defect (row-exact + PK-unique is the real gate).** **(W5) `at` is a DuckDB RESERVED word (→`at_`); a CTE named the SAME as its base table self-references in DuckDB (→rename e.g. `team_ref`); the `{% if is_incremental() %}…{% else %}<real where>{% endif %}` else-arm must be HAND-INLINED (the runner's stripper eats it); a literal `{% else %}` inside a SQL `--` comment BREAKS `dbtf compile` ("unknown statement else"); `dbt_utils.date_spine()` can't survive the extractor → inline a DuckDB `range()`; match the retired table's TYPE (`mart_game_results`=DATE, `mart_game_spine`=TIMESTAMP_NTZ — cast `game_date::date`/`::timestamp`); incremental→view = just drop the `incremental` config + the `is_incremental()` WHERE arms (full rebuild). 🐞 **INCREMENTAL TYPE-DRIFT (recurring — INC-15/W1d, INC-16-P0, INC-19 2026-06-29):** when a dual-branch change makes a feature column compute as a DIFFERENT type than the EXISTING Snowflake incremental table (classic: DuckDB FLOAT vs an existing `NUMBER(38,x)`), the incremental run FAILS — `cannot change column … from NUMBER(38,x) to FLOAT` — and HALTs the job. **FIX: manually `DROP` the affected incremental table(s) (+ any downstream model carrying the column) → rebuild fresh** (`--full-refresh` is UNRELIABLE in dbt-fusion — it MERGEs). **PREVENT: CAST the column to a consistent type in the dual-branch model** (DuckDB + Snowflake agree) so the type can't drift. ⚠️ every `feature_pregame_*` incremental model is a W8 candidate for this — cast consistently as you flip each to a DuckDB branch. PARITY-PK: pick the TRUE grain — `mart_home_away_splits` is per-GAME not per-date → PK `(game_pk, team)` (doubleheaders collide on `(team, flag, game_date)`). **(W5b) Snowflake `lateral flatten(input => variant_obj)` → DuckDB list-comprehension unnest (`unnest([{...} for k in json_keys(probs)])`); a direct `cast(... as MAP)` on VARCHAR-JSON FAILS. `matched` is a DuckDB reserved word (MERGE). For Bayesian/k-means TOLERANCE-class migrations: seed-pin (`random_state`), the SEEDED cutover is value-exact (parity row-exact-grade); the ~3rd-decimal band only bites on a DuckDB REBUILD → parity check both paths (drift bands + MAP-cluster agreement ≥98%).** **🧮 BUILDER DUAL-WRITE RULE:** when you migrate a computed-table BUILDER's I/O to `--s3`, that's ADDITIVE if non-migrated consumers (feature layer, deferred marts) still read its Snowflake output → KEEP the Snowflake builder run until those consumers migrate; the builder's Snowflake compute is only ELIMINATED once nothing reads its Snowflake table (track this for the cost AC).
**DISCIPLINE (makes fast safe):** per-mart VALUE-PRESERVING parity BEFORE the view swap (this caught 3 latent serving bugs W1d shipped silently); P6 alerting + the P5 CD auto-rollback are the net. 🚨 **GRANT-PRESERVATION (INC-18, 2026-06-29):** every `CREATE OR REPLACE VIEW/TABLE` SILENTLY DROPS Snowflake GRANTs → any object on the request-time fallback path (read by `app/backend/routers/picks.py`/`bets.py`) loses `CREDENCE_API_RO`'s SELECT on recreate → cache-miss 503. INC-18 added schema FUTURE GRANTS + a staging `+post-hook` re-grant in `dbt_project.yml`; **any wave recreating a request-read object MUST confirm its schema has the FUTURE GRANTS (or a post-hook re-grant)** + verify a Snowflake-fallback request returns 200 post-cutover. 🪪 **BOTO3 INSTANCE-ROLE FALLBACK (W7b-1, 2026-06-29 — cost a morning):** on the EC2 box S3 auth is the **instance IAM role** (post-INC-16); `AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID` is UNSET. **NEVER pass `aws_access_key_id=os.environ.get("AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID")` to boto3** — passing `None` DISABLES boto3's default credential chain → `AuthorizationHeaderMalformed`. Pass explicit keys ONLY if present, else fall back to the chain (or use DuckDB `COPY` / a shared `s3_client()` helper). Any NEW boto3 S3 writer must follow this. Mirror/parity-only ops must be **mirror-tier (ALERT-continue), NOT HALT**, until their cutover flag flips. **CUTOVER ORDER (P5 CD live):** build S3 parquet → `parity GREEN` → create the `lakehouse_ext` external tables in Snowflake → THEN commit/PR (merge auto-deploys via CD on `dbt/**`+`scripts/**`) → verify post-deploy. **A precursor (getting a non-mart Snowflake SOURCE into S3) comes before its marts.**
**SEQUENCING:** the mart GROUPS are independent, but every wave edits the SHARED build scripts (`run_w1_lakehouse.py`/`refresh`/the DDL generator) → run **W4→W5→W6→W7 SEQUENTIALLY** (one Opus session each, each builds on the prior's shared-script state) to avoid shared-file merge conflicts. **W7 (readers) is LAST** — it needs every mart it consumes already in S3.

GUARDS (serving path): (1) ATOMIC today-partition swap (write-then-register; a failed rewrite leaves the prior good partition live — never serve a half-written partition); (2) the partition-aware external table must UNION all partitions (today+history) + the read sees today's partition immediately post-rewrite; (3) parity the FULL table ONCE after the initial partitioned build, then the intraday delta = today's partition only; (4) idempotent today-overwrite each cycle. 🎯 **REQUEST-TIME marts are HERE:** the W4 audit put the request-time-FALLBACK reads in this subtree — `mart_odds_outcomes`/`mart_game_odds_bridge` are read in the EV/picks/game-detail fallback (P2b fixed `/picks/ev` already). (3) **Exercise the 4 wins that justify Delta:** (a) SCHEMA-EVOLUTION `ALTER`/add-col doesn't HALT (the INC-19 cure, structural); (b) MERGE-into-partition = an incremental update with NO full rebuild (the `run_w1_lakehouse` 40-min driver); (c) RETENTION/COMPACTION / snapshot-expiration (the INC-20 cure); (d) TIME-TRAVEL "as of date X" (the leakage-audit / point-in-time asset). (4) ⚠️ **MODEL-I/O BOUNDARY:** write up the recommended **Polars→pandas conversion at `model.predict()`** (sklearn expects pandas — the E11.20 gotcha), even if this table doesn't serve. (5) **MEASURE vs the Parquet baseline:** write/read latency, storage, incremental-update time (Delta MERGE vs full rebuild), ergonomics.
🔒 SCOPE DISCIPLINE: ONE table, POC ONLY. Do NOT convert the lakehouse, do NOT touch serving, do NOT big-bang Polars. Box gotchas apply (`BOX_OPERATIONS.md`).

(3) 💰 **COST — kill the residual Snowflake warehouse burn (operator 2026-07-07: still ~$55/day):** every `lakehouse_ext.*` read spins a warehouse. **Delta-on-path is read DIRECTLY by DuckDB/Polars (`delta_scan`) = ZERO Snowflake warehouse spin** → migrating a table to Delta structurally removes its ext-table read cost, not just its incident risk. ⇒ **so success is NOT just "Delta's structural wins" — it MUST show a MEASURED runtime reduction AND a MEASURED Snowflake-credit reduction.**

▶ INC-22 — 🔴 P1 SERVING BUG: `write_serving_store_intraday_op` computes TOMORROW's date (UTC-midnight rollover) → evening intraday refresh silently doesn't run   [Serving · 🧭 OPUS · ⭐ ASSIGNED 2026-06-29 as the 3rd parallel session · diagnose-and-fix · parallel-SAFE with W8a + W12]   (2026-06-29, live P1)
🚨 THE BUG (observed 2026-06-29 ~19:12 CDT = 00:12 UTC 6/30): `write_serving_store_intraday_op` resolved **date=2026-06-30** while the live slate is **6/29** → "No predictions for 2026-06-30 — skipping picks/today/featured/ev" + "0 game_pks" + a misleading `ops/heartbeat#daily date=2026-06-30 n_picks=0`. ROOT (prime hypothesis): the op derives "today" from **UTC** (`datetime.utcnow().date()` / `datetime.now(timezone.utc).date()`) and the box runs UTC → after ~00:00 UTC (= evening US time) it rolls to tomorrow, but predictions + `game_date` are keyed to the **US baseball-day**. The MORNING op is immune (runs ~13:00 UTC = still 6/29 UTC); only the EVENING intraday ops cross the boundary.
IMPACT: not a clobber (the skip-on-empty guard protected the 6/29 picks cache — good) BUT (a) tonight's 6/29 intraday price/lineup refresh DID NOT RUN → evening slate goes stale in the app; (b) a false 6/30 `n_picks=0` heartbeat (could mislead the dead-man monitor / metrics).
⚡ **IMMEDIATE MITIGATION (do first if the op supports it):** re-run the intraday write with an explicit date override for **2026-06-29** (e.g. `--date 2026-06-29`) to refresh tonight's slate NOW, while building the durable fix. If no override flag exists, that's part of the fix.
DO:
 1. **Find the date derivation** in `write_serving_store.py` (the intraday path) + the op wrapper in `pipeline/ops/`. Confirm it's UTC-based. Check the MORNING vs INTRADAY ops for the inconsistency (morning coincidentally-correct, intraday wrong).
 2. **Identify the CANONICAL baseball-day TZ** the rest of the path uses so dates JOIN — `predict_today` / `mart_game_odds_bridge.game_date` / the `mart_odds_outcomes` `_history`/`_current` split (INC-21 #5 noted that split is on **LA-today**). At 00:12 UTC every US TZ is still 6/29, but pick the one the marts/predictions key on (likely `America/New_York` ET game-date or `America/Los_Angeles`) so the serving date matches the prediction date — confirm by reading, don't assume.
 3. **Route ALL serving/predict "today" through ONE helper** (a canonical `current_game_date()` in the configured TZ) + add the `--date` override. Grep the serving/predict/intraday path for `utcnow().date()` / `date.today()` / `now(timezone.utc).date()` and repoint every site.
 4. **Recurrence guard:** a freeze-time unit test at 00:30 UTC asserting the serving date = the US baseball-day (6/29), not 6/30 — so this can't regress. Also make the empty-because-wrong-date case ALERT-loud (it currently looks like a benign skip — exactly how it hid).
🤝 COORDINATION: touches the serving-write/date-helper path — NOT `feature_pregame_*`/`gen_type_contract.py` (W8a) and NOT sensor files (W12). If it needs a shared `pipeline/` util, check for a W12 collision first.
AC: the intraday op resolves the correct US baseball-day across the UTC-midnight boundary (freeze-time test proves it), all serving/predict "today" sites route through the one canonical helper, a `--date` override exists, the wrong-date-empty case alerts instead of silently skipping, tonight's 6/29 slate refreshed via the mitigation, CI green (fast gate). Operator handoff: the fixed op + the helper + the test + confirmation the evening intraday cycle now runs on the right date + `git add`. ⚠️ this is the same TZ-boundary CLASS as INC-21 #5 (LA-vs-UTC date split) — note any other UTC `today` you find in the serving path.

First look: `uv run python scripts/ops/model_health_metrics.py --since 2026-06-10 --prediction-type post_lineup --schema betting_ml`.
🥇 **PRIME HYPOTHESIS — a SERVING/FEATURE regression, NOT model decay** (the window overlaps the lakehouse-migration period + the recent serving bugs):
 • **Precedent:** W1d's woba-zero bug ZEROED the H2H matchup features from ~06-25 until W2 fixed it ~06-26 — exactly the class of corruption that kills `home_win` discrimination. The 06-10→06-28 window STRADDLES that.
 • **Decisive test:** is the corr still bad AFTER ~06-26 (post-woba-fix)? Slice the window — if discrimination RECOVERS post-fix → it WAS the woba bug (this alert is a lagging echo, window-averaged); if STILL bad after 06-26 → a separate/ongoing regression (suspect: the W2/W3/W3-main mart migrations or the +5h time / settle bugs fed bad features/labels).
 • **Served-input vs model:** re-score the SAME games offline with KNOWN-GOOD (training-time) features → if discrimination returns, it's a SERVING/FEATURE-PIPELINE regression (a migrated mart serving NULL/zeroed/stale feature values), NOT the model. This is the fork that decides everything.
OTHER HYPOTHESES (rule out): (2) label/eval artifact — does `model_health_metrics.py` join the served prediction to the RIGHT outcome post-lakehouse (a `mart_game_results`/`daily_model_predictions` join or TZ/date bug — cf. E9.34 — could mis-pair pred↔outcome and fake a collapse)? (3) calibration drift (unlikely — corr is DISCRIMINATION, not calibration); (4) genuine distribution shift / model decay (only conclude after 1–3 are excluded).
TIE-IN: the W4–W7 decommission waves touch the feature substrate → their value-preserving parity gates should PREVENT new feature corruption, but **once the dust settles, re-verify served feature values match the training distribution** (parity on the FEATURE values the model consumed, not just mart row counts). If this resolves to feature corruption, add a served-feature-integrity check to the model-health suite so it's caught at the input, not via downstream discrimination.

Honest framing: this is the served model's core discrimination claim → P1.

▶ INC-16-P6a   ✅ DONE 2026-06-28 (committed + pushed `dev` → PR→main→P5 CD). **Two-layer suppression:** (1) **deploy-lock** — `deploy.sh` writes `/tmp/credence_deploy_in_progress` (after sourcing notify, before any work) + `trap rm EXIT` (clears on success/die/rollback); `healthcheck.sh` SKIPs + resets the fail counter while it exists. (2) **debounce** — `/tmp/credence_healthcheck_fail_count` increments per fail, pages only at `FAIL_THRESHOLD=3` consecutive (~15 min), resets to 0 on any success (overridable `HEALTHCHECK_FAIL_THRESHOLD`). ▶ Story prompt — INC-16-P6a P6 healthcheck FALSE-POSITIVE — "core service(s) down" pages during CD deploys   [Infra/SRE · 🧭 OPUS (small/contained) · P2 alert-hygiene · P6 follow-on · ships via P5 CD]   (2026-06-28, operator)
WHY: `healthcheck.sh` paged CRITICAL **4× in 12h** listing `dagster-codeloc`/`-daemon`/`-webserver`/`dbt-runner` "container down" — but the box is healthy (FALSE POSITIVE). Cry-wolf CRITICALs erode trust in the REAL P6 alerts (dead-man switch, the INC-17 model-health alert) → fix the noise.
🥇 **ROOT CAUSE (diagnosed):** the 4 flagged services are EXACTLY the app-image containers the **P5 CD rebuilds** on a `dbt/**`/`scripts/**`/`pipeline/**` merge (`docker compose up -d --build`); `dagster-postgres`/`flaresolverr`/`caddy` (NOT rebuilt) stayed healthy → that's why they're absent from the alert. The 5-min host-cron `healthcheck.sh` step-1 check `docker compose ps --status running --services` lands DURING the recreate window → those 4 are momentarily `restarting`/`created`, not `running` → false "container down". **4 alerts ≈ 4 merges/deploys today** (W3pre, W3-main, E9.34, …), each >1h apart so each clears the 1h cooldown. (NOT the cwd/compose-file gotcha — the script already uses the explicit `-f`.)
FIX (combine, in `services/dagster/aws/healthcheck.sh` + `deploy.sh`):
 1. **Debounce — require ≥2 (ideally 3) CONSECUTIVE failed checks before paging.** Keep a small counter state file (increment on fail, reset to 0 on success); page only when it crosses the threshold. A transient single-check deploy blip won't page; a REAL sustained outage stays failed across checks → still pages (preserve true-positive). This is the robust general fix.
 2. **Deploy-aware suppression:** `deploy.sh` writes a lock (e.g. `/tmp/credence_deploy_in_progress`) at start + removes it in a trap on exit; `healthcheck.sh` SKIPs (or resets the counter, doesn't page) while the lock exists. Directly kills the deploy-window race even if a deploy spans >1 check.
 3. (Optional, sharper liveness) treat `restarting`/`created`/`recreating`/`health: starting` as TRANSIENT (not "down") via `docker inspect` State/Health — only `exited`/`dead`/missing = real down. Step-2's `compose exec … curl` into codeloc also fails mid-recreate → the debounce covers it.
GUARD — don't over-suppress: a genuinely-stopped container (`docker compose stop dagster-daemon` left down across ≥ threshold checks) MUST still page within ~10–15 min.
VERIFY: (a) trigger a real CD deploy (or `up -d --build`) → confirm NO page; (b) stop a core container and leave it → confirm it DOES page after the consecutive-fail threshold; (c) confirm the dead-man switch + other P6 alerts unaffected.
Read: `services/dagster/aws/healthcheck.sh` (the step-1 `ps --status running` + the cooldown), `services/dagster/aws/deploy.sh` (the `up -d --build` window — add the lock), `capture.crontab` (the 5-min line).
➕ **ALSO (optional, same theme — P6 alerting trustworthiness; from P2b 2026-06-28):** `write_serving_store` was found SILENTLY falling to S3-only when its DynamoDB write failed (an IAM gap swallowed as an exception → the cache went stale invisibly). Add a LOUD signal: on a DynamoDB write failure, emit a WARNING/alert (via `pipeline/utils/alerting.py`) instead of quietly continuing S3-only — so a serving-write degradation pages rather than hides. (Small; fold in if scope allows, else flag as a separate P6 follow-on.)
Gate/AC: no false page during a CD deploy (verified on a real deploy); real sustained outage still pages within ~15 min; debounce + deploy-lock in place; ships via P5 CD; `bash -n` clean. Operator handoff: the change + the verification evidence (a clean deploy with no page + a real-stop that does page).

▶ Story prompt — INC-18-fix Remove STAGING tables from the request path (the durable INC-18 fix)   [App/backend · 🧭 SONNET · 🟡 P2 tech-debt (band-aid already holds) · bake-off-EXEMPT · NOW FOLDED INTO W7]   (2026-06-29, from INC-18)

The shipped post-hook + schema FUTURE GRANTS are a durable BAND-AID (so this is P2, not on-fire) — but the ROOT anti-pattern is that the serving fallback queries **STAGING** at all. Staging is rebuilt constantly (every W-wave + daily build); MARTS are the stable serving interface. Close it so a routine rebuild can NEVER 503 serving again. 🌐 read order is DynamoDB→S3→**Snowflake (last-resort fallback)**; the goal = that last tier reads MARTS, not `stg_*`.

2. **For any `stg_*` with NO clean mart equivalent:** do NOT force a bad repoint or invent a half-baked mart in this story — KEEP that read, ensure it's covered by the FUTURE GRANTS/post-hook (it is), and FLAG it in the handoff as needing a thin serving-mart (a follow-up). Report how many fell in this bucket.
3. **Keep the INC-18 band-aid IN PLACE** (FUTURE GRANTS + the staging post-hook) as defense-in-depth — this refactor reduces the surface, the grants stay as backstop.

So daily billed ≈ `compute_credits + MAX(0, cloud_services_credits − 0.10 × compute_credits)`, summed over the period (apply the adjustment DAILY, not on the period total). The Admin currently sums cloud-services credits straight → wrong (too high). ℹ️ this reads Snowflake's OWN metering (`SNOWFLAKE.ACCOUNT_USAGE.METERING_*` / warehouse_metering) — a **SANCTIONED Snowflake read** (billing metadata, not lakehouse data; exception to the off-Snowflake rule). ▶ Story prompt — E5.8 FanGraphs Stuff+ ROLLING WINDOWS for pitching (surface the 14d/30d Stuff+/Location+/Pitching+ trend the ingest ALREADY pulls but the model throws away) + de-leak the season-to-date join   [Model/data · 🧭 OPUS/SONNET · feature-availability + point-in-time de-leak · touches the serving-critical starter feature → VALIDATE, don't just plumb]   (2026-07-04, from the E11.1-W11-FG rolling-window audit + operator ask)

So the rolling PULLS happen; the rolling STRUCTURE is discarded for pitching Stuff+. (Rolling *Statcast* pitching — velo/CSW/pitch-mix/TTO — is separately well-covered via `mart_pitcher_rolling_stats`/`mart_starter_*_rolling`; this gap is specifically the FanGraphs Stuff+ arsenal-quality grade.)
🔗 DOUBLE VALUE — this ALSO fixes a KNOWN LEAK: the E1.11′/feature-leakage-audit (`ablation_results/feature_leakage_audit.md`, §7.2) flagged the Stuff+ block as **🟥 LEAKY-season-to-date** — joined `season = year(game_date)` with NO `< game_date` guard, so the full-season Stuff+ value embeds game-G-and-later pitches (hits `home_starter_stuff_plus`, `away_starter_avg_fastball_velo`). A proper AS-OF rolling window (strictly-prior trailing snapshot per game) is point-in-time-safe BY CONSTRUCTION → the rolling rebuild is the natural home for the de-leak. Do BOTH in one pass (don't ship a rolling feature that's still leak-joined downstream).
DO: (1) TAG the window in the raw + ingest — add `window_type`/`window_start`/`window_end` to `fg_stuff_plus_raw` (DDL) + the `ingest_fangraphs_stuff_plus.py` row dict (the ingest already HAS these values per-window; it just isn't storing them — mirror `ingest_fangraphs_hitting_leaderboard.py`). Backfill history if the windows are recoverable from `request_params` (startdate/enddate) else re-ingest. (2) PRESERVE in `stg_fangraphs__stuff_plus` — repartition the dedup on `(fg_pitcher_id, season, window_type, window_start)` (mirror `stg_fangraphs__hitting_leaderboard`) so each rolling window survives; keep BOTH the DuckDB + Snowflake dual-branch (this is now W4-lakehouse — see E11.1-W11-FG). (3) PIVOT in `fct_fangraphs_pitching_analytics` — add `rolling_stuff_plus_14d/30d`, `rolling_location_plus_*`, `rolling_pitching_plus_*`, `season_stuff_plus` (mirror the hitting fct's `max(case when window_type=... )` pivot). ⚠️ this EXTENDS the fct schema → regenerate the W4 external table (`generate_w4_external_tables.py` → `w4_external_tables.generated.sql`) + `refresh_w1_external_tables --w4`; INC-19 type-pin discipline if any NUMBER↔FLOAT. (4) CONSUME + DE-LEAK in `feature_pregame_starter_features` — swap the leaky `season = year(game_date)` Stuff+ join for the AS-OF rolling window (strictly-prior), exposing the trend features. (5) VALIDATE (serving-critical feature → NOT just plumbing): run the E13.4 lift harness / a purged-embargoed A/B to confirm rolling Stuff+ trend adds signal over season-to-date (and that the de-leak doesn't regress the offline number in a way that reveals prior leakage inflation); PBO<0.2/DSR>0; `best_alpha=0` honesty. A null (rolling adds nothing) is a fine, informative result — but the DE-LEAK ships regardless (correctness).
⚠️ LANDMINES (inherit E11.1-W11-FG's): W4-lakehouse dual-branch (DuckDB `json_extract_string` flatten; SF else = `lakehouse_ext`); the VALUE:-case + binary-ts→VARCHAR ext-table rules; parity is necessary-NOT-sufficient (per-ROW ext fetch + real `--w4` build); `feature_pregame_starter_features` is a W8b serving-critical model → the box cutover order matters (build the fct parquet BEFORE the W8b feature build reads it).
Gate/AC: rolling Stuff+ windows surfaced in `fct_fangraphs_pitching_analytics` (parity with the hitting fct's rolling structure) + the season-to-date leak REMOVED from `feature_pregame_starter_features` (as-of join) + the lift/validation result (signal or trustworthy null) + CI green (fast pytest + both dbt jobs) + the W4 ext-table regen. Operator handoff: the `fg_stuff_plus_raw` DDL migration + re-ingest/backfill + `--w4` rebuild + ext regen + the validation gate result. Ties to E11.1-W11-FG (same W4 fangraphs subtree), the E1.11′ leak-audit §7.2, and the E13.x temporal/recency-signal thread (Stuff+/velo TREND).
